Father! I earnestly hope and wish to be your sons and daughters who are not lacking in welcoming the year 1965. Father, there have been many twists and turns in the path you have led humanity, and there have been many sad events along the way you have taken, so how could the children who follow you know your love? 

We have had the story of carrying the historical sins of our ancestors before you and sighing, but now we must remember that this is the time of victory. We earnestly hope and wish that you will allow us to keep this in mind. 

Please do not let us become those who will shed tears in the future for failing to fulfill the responsibilities entrusted to us in our time. We must not forget the mission entrusted to us by you and must be determined once again to be your sons and daughters who will struggle to take responsibility for it, no matter what happens. 

Please awaken our dull minds, heal our sick spirits, and raise our fallen bodies so that we can have the determination, conviction, and heart of oath to receive and fulfill the words you command. We earnestly hope and wish for this. 

Father, may this day be a day that can be remembered. We have come joyfully, so please satisfy that heart and let us return with a strong resolution. Thus, may we discover that our hearts and bodies are needed before heaven, and may we be true filial sons and daughters who can fulfill our responsibilities and struggle to understand your heart. 

Father, I earnestly hope and wish for this. We entrust all of ourselves to you who have come to us, and we will not part from our Father, we will hold onto our Father's love, and we will deeply carry our Father's circumstances and ideals, and we will struggle and cry out that we will dwell deep in our Father's heart. 

Father, may we be those who reaffirm our commitment before your command. While finishing this year, may we also have the glory of victors joyfully welcoming a new day, and may we be your sons and daughters who can comply with the mission entrusted to us and fulfill the responsibilities of priests. 

We entrust this entire time before you, so please be with us. 

On this day, your children scattered overseas are shedding tears toward this place, and you know their hearts that long only for your love, so please comfort them. In the environment where circumstances are not favorable, please grant them a heart of consolation as they hope for joy and a day of hope. We earnestly hope and wish that you will grant once again the new grace of our Father that can promise happiness on this day and this time. 

There are also your children who are fighting in lonely places while walking lonely paths in various parts of South Korea, so please be with them. If they are trembling in cold places, please remember them, and as you have commanded me, command them too, and be with them. We earnestly hope that they will not lack in fulfilling their national mission on the remaining path of restoration. 

Are there children with little faith here today? Please personally govern their hearts and bodies. May this time be one where they can offer their bodies as not their own but as offerings before you, and may all their thoughts and everything they have be offered directly before you, so that they may move according to your desires, your providence, and your commands. 

Thus, may their bodies and hearts be completely captured before you at this time, and may they be raised as children who can receive your promises. 

The time is approaching when the will and ideals you hope for, regarding the final day, must be determined through us, so I earnestly hope and wish to be your sons and daughters who can act boldly with confidence before that. 

On this day, please bless the countless altars that call upon your name, and be with the many religious people who seek the path of goodness, willing to offer themselves as sacrifices, regardless of the paths of death or suffering, calling upon your name and seeking to follow your will. 

I earnestly hope and wish that you will allow the many conscientious people preparing for the promised day not to miss that day of promise. 

Now, we entrust the remaining entirety before you, so please personally govern it. We earnestly ask and wish that your joyful will and desires may be with us for a long time. In all these words, we earnestly pray in the name of the Lord. Amen. 

<Words> When the Feast of Tabernacles, a Jewish holiday, was near, his brothers said to Jesus, “Leave here and go to Judea, so that your disciples may see the works you are doing. No one who wants to become a public figure acts in secret. Since you are doing these things, show yourself to the world.” (John 7:3-4) From this, we can see that the whole family did not believe in or welcome Jesus. 

The life of Jesus left behind sorrow, pain, and resentment. 

For Jesus, who had to realize the tremendous will to resolve God's will and the fate of the nation, the family should have been the primary stepping stone, yet that family was shattered. Consequently, Jesus had no choice but to leave home. 

Everyone! If you doubt this, pray. When the holidays came and there was food, his brothers would hide it among themselves and ostracize Jesus. However, Jesus did not long for food. More than that, when he saw people celebrating the holiday, nestled in their parents' arms and holding their parents' hands, he felt an indescribable longing for such moments. 

In achieving a great mission and a great will, for the first time in history, Jesus wished to establish a family that God desired on the foundation of the Joseph family and to create a foundation that could include John the Baptist based on Jesus' relatives. Nevertheless, as that family fell apart and parents, brothers, and relatives left, Jesus found himself without a place to go. 

You must understand that Jesus' second journey was to find John the Baptist. When Jesus lost his family and began his public ministry, he left with a sorrowful heart more than anyone else. He had great hopes for the family based on the heavenly principles, yet he had to abandon that family, and who could understand the lonely heart he felt? However, he did not speak of these difficulties to anyone. In his heart, he only looked forward to the day of victory, saying, "When that day comes, I will let you know." 

While he had an unexpressed solemn determination externally, we must not forget that sorrow dwelled in his heart. 

With this sorrowful heart, John the Baptist testified about Jesus by baptizing him in the Jordan River. However, the followers of John the Baptist did not fulfill their duty of devotion and loyalty, and they ended up separating from Jesus. From God's perspective, they were in the position of an external family, that is, a Cain-like family, and they did not understand Jesus' internal feelings and intentions, leading to their separation. 

Thus, the environment became one where the disciples of John the Baptist and the disciples of Jesus had no choice but to quarrel. You must understand how resentful this fact was. 

As a result, Jesus could not even focus on his family. He received testimony from John the Baptist, whom God had established, but he could not give his heart to him. The hope of creating an external fence centered around John the Baptist to manage the whole was shattered. Consequently, Jesus had no choice but to turn to Judaism. You must understand that Jesus went to Judaism to rectify even the mistakes of John the Baptist, yet Judaism also betrayed Jesus. 

Then, Jesus turned away from the Judaism that rejected him and sought out the nation that opposed his sect. If that nation had been an independent country, a sovereign state, he would have sought out the king or the sovereign of that nation. However, at that time, the nation had lost its sovereignty and had become a Roman colony, and Jesus found himself in a position where he could not oppose Rome, so you must understand that an indescribable resentment dwelled in his heart. 

You must understand that Jesus left behind sorrow, pain, and resentment in his 33 years of life, and he did not leave behind hope, happiness, or purpose. Such a Jesus could not give his heart to the nation, nor to the sect, nor to the prophet John the Baptist whom God had established, nor to his family. 

In this position, Jesus had no choice but to wander from one town to another, from one street to another, from the Jews to the Gentiles, and from one family to another. Thus, he lamented, “Foxes have dens and birds have nests, but the Son of Man has no place to lay his head.” (Matthew 8:20) 

In light of this fact, you must clearly understand that while Jesus had nowhere to go and nowhere to come back to, he had to bear the responsibilities and missions he was entrusted with and suffer internally. 

Jesus, who was driven away from his family, John the Baptist, and the Jewish sect, where was he to go? He had no choice but to seek the most miserable place. In that era, those who stood in places welcomed by many people were disheartened, and they had to seek out those who were in humble positions. 

Why did Jesus have to preach the good news to the poor? Jesus came to this earth with the mission to gather those in the highest positions and to rebuild the nation of Israel, yet he ended up seeking the miserable multitude instead of fulfilling the national expectations. This is something that should be mourned and lamented deeply in Christianity today. 

You must engrave this fact deeply in your hearts. 

As Jesus sought out those humble places, he longed for the day when he could gather the nation and the people of Israel, seize the nations scattered all over the world, judge evil, and make all enemy nations surrender, offering a glorious sacrifice before the Father. How much did he long for that day of unity and victory? 

The great hope, the great responsibility, and the great mission were all abandoned by the family, the followers of John the Baptist, and Judaism, and from the leaders of that era.
In such an environment, twisted beyond recognition by receiving the cross, the internal struggles I had to manage were more than a few hundred times greater than those of a person walking a smooth path. We must recognize that Jesus, who had to carry such struggles, was both pitiful and sorrowful.

Why did Jesus have to offer such a poignant prayer before God at the foot of the Mount of Olives, and why did he have to wander from street to street? Why did he have to confront the group of traitors wherever he went? If this is a riddle, it is indeed a riddle; yet, from a human perspective, it is something that could happen, but from heaven's viewpoint, it is a frustrating and lamentable fact. We must think again about how grave the responsibility of Judaism was in committing such acts, how significant the responsibility of John the Baptist was, and how great the responsibilities of Joseph's household and Mary were.

Jesus had nowhere to go. Even the steps he took to find uneducated fishermen like Peter and James were blocked by his own people, leaving him with no place to go. There was no way to break through; he could not abandon the nation of Israel to go to the Gentiles. The foundation upon which God had labored for 4,000 years, centered on the providence of restoration, was the nation of Israel. Therefore, he had to lead them internally, even if they had made mistakes. Although the nation was at fault, if he could establish them in any way in the areas for which they were responsible, he might be able to inherit something before God. Until that inheritance was received, Jesus was one who could not go anywhere.

Jesus came to possess the world, to embrace heaven and earth, to be the sovereign who would govern all mankind, and to be the central being through whom the glory of the ages would be realized on earth; yet he lost all of this. He came to give all the glory of heaven to this earth, but because the nation of Israel betrayed him, it was a situation where he could not give it. Nevertheless, we must understand the unjust and resentful circumstances that compelled Jesus to embrace them. He was Jesus, who ventured forth with the hope of the world and the hope of humanity. Yet, when he looked at the unfaithful nation of Israel, he felt a desire to curse them, but he could not do so. Why? Because if Jesus, who bore the historical responsibility, cursed the nation of Israel, it would mean that the labor of God over 4,000 years would be utterly shattered. The downfall of Israel is not what is frustrating and lamentable; it is the breaking of God's labor.

If he could not grasp what he intended to hold in his right hand, he had to at least grasp it with his left hand and move forward, clashing with the world to inherit the will and the foundation that God had left behind, ensuring that he left behind some condition to restore it. He wanted to curse the nation of Israel and Judaism that had caused him such frustration and resentment, but because of that situation, he had to grit his teeth and move forward. Who could understand his heart?

The Sadness of Jesus, Who Could Not Unite with His Disciples
How great was God's labor in bringing forth the nation of Israel, which had to resolve all of God's wishes and historical grievances? God protected them whenever they walked the path of suffering, fearing they might be hurt. When God led them out as a group to be remembered for generations, and when the historical foundation that could move the whole was opposed to Jesus, the personal sorrow of Jesus was great, but he could not lift his head before the merit of God's labor.

When Jesus stood at the fateful path where he had to go to the Garden of Gethsemane, the crowds opposing him may have rejoiced, but the hopes of God, who had established him, and the hopes of the people who followed him were shattered. Jesus naturally felt sorrow and pain for himself, and he could endure that difficulty, but he was saddened by the fact that all of God's labor, which had sought him for 4,000 years, was being shattered.

God became the offering in the historical process of pioneering the path, and while he remained in all the labor's process, Jesus, looking at the nation of Israel and the Jewish community, which had not fulfilled their responsibilities in reality, must have felt a curse and resentment proportional to God's expectations. However, because there was a situation where he could not turn curses toward them, he went to the Garden of Gethsemane, thinking about the responsibility to leave behind a condition before the nation and the world. Many Christians today, who claim to be brides, do not understand the circumstances of Jesus.

Jesus lost all of the twelve disciples, who had shared joys and sorrows with him for over three years, saying, "Where you go is where we hope to go, and where you are is where we seek to be, and the place where you live is the foundation of our happiness. We will live and die with you." Thus, Jesus, who was left with an indescribable heart and a lonely feeling that he could not share with anyone, was chased by the nation and went to the Mount of Olives or the Garden of Gethsemane to pray alone. You must truly understand the heart of Jesus in that situation.

God sent his only begotten son to this earth to change it into a foundation of happiness, but because he found himself in a position of sorrow, he left behind a nail in God's heart. Jesus felt he had no face to show God. He was the Savior of Israel who came to restore the nation of Israel, and he was the king of Israel, yet he lost the nation and was heading toward the Garden of Gethsemane to settle accounts with God. You must not forget this.

Jesus was a pitiful orphan of heaven and earth. He was like the most pitiful orphan who could not find a place to rest his heart anywhere on this earth. While everyone has feelings of sorrow and joy, Jesus was a lonely being who could not find a single object of joy. Thus, he was the most sorrowful orphan in history. This is not to speak of the world but to view it in light of God's will and Jesus' mission and responsibility. He was a being of unspeakable loneliness. Therefore, he felt he had no face to call God "Father." What must have been the heart of Jesus, who vowed not to leave, as he called out to his Father in the Garden of Gethsemane? Even though his cells were racing and his bones were melting, the three disciples who had been with him for three years fell asleep. Not being able to endure even for an hour and not participating in that moment is, as a human who should have welcomed the Messiah, the most lamentable fact.

What if the disciples had resonated with Jesus' sorrow and clung to his garment, weeping with him? Christianity would not have become so miserable. If they had died alongside him as his chief disciples, they would have been resurrected. Because they failed to fulfill their responsibilities before the Messiah who came for all humanity, Christianity after Jesus' departure became a miserable religion. Whose sin is this? It is the sin of the three disciples who failed in their responsibilities.

What Kind of Bride Does the Lord Desire?
Then, in what position do you wish to seek the Messiah? In what position do you want to meet the bridegroom Jesus? What kind of preparation and what kind of appearance do you wish to present before him? This is a rather serious issue in today's reality. Will Jesus desire a bride who welcomes him with splendidly prepared lamps of glory, saying, "You are my bridegroom"? Or will he desire a bride who, in a lonely place like the Garden of Gethsemane, weeps and embraces the rising emotions, saying, "Our ancestors failed to fulfill their responsibilities"? How will you answer?

The Lord seeks a bride of suffering before meeting a bride of glory. You must go through the relationship of being a bride of suffering to qualify as a bride here. This is the path of restoration. To shed the father's sorrow, the child must go out to a place of sorrow greater than the father's sorrow.

If Jesus came to this earth to welcome a bride, what kind of bride would he desire? He would want a bride who knows everything he has not been able to say until now and can comfort him by understanding all that is bound in his heart. Furthermore, he will seek a bride who can resolve and comfort the grievances and pains bound in God's heart. Look, God, who had to abandon the nation of Israel, which he had chosen as his people and had labored for 4,000 years amidst unspeakable suffering and toil, sent his one and only begotten son as the Messiah for that nation. Yet, he still had to bless a nation that betrayed him. He is in a position where he cannot do either, and he will seek a bride who can comfort God's heart in such a situation.

Who is Jesus? He is the prince sent by God. He is the king sent by God. What qualifications must a person have to become a bride before the Messiah, who comes as the prince? They must be someone who can relate to him both internally and externally. Just as he loves humanity, the bride must also love humanity; just as he cares for God, the bride must also care for God; just as he bears responsibility for the present world and the future, the bride must also bear responsibility.

Those who wish to become such brides should not first pray for blessings. They should first pray, "Please give me your wrath." Why? Because they betrayed Jesus, who came to give blessings, and they must sacrifice themselves to atone for that historical sin and resolve that grievance. A bride must say, "Before I ask for forgiveness for my sins, I must first say, 'Please forgive the historical sins.'"

Only those who are determined to uproot the very roots of the sins committed by Adam and Eve, bearing the sorrow, pain, and twists of fate, and are willing to atone for all of it can become brides.

That is why Jesus said, "Anyone who loves father or mother more than me is not worthy of me, and anyone who loves son or daughter more than me is not worthy of me." (Matthew 10:37) What does it mean to say you love a thousand times? You must love with your body, with your heart, and even more, with your spirit. Words cannot transcend the limits of the times. However, when viewed through the mission of Jesus, he transcended the limits of the times. He came with a heavenly mission that represented the past, present, and future, and all the ideals that sprang from his heart were historical. Among the tears he shed were tears that could represent individuals, families, nations, and the world. He should have been able to rejoice, yet he could not. That joy was not centered on the individual; it had to encompass the chosen people of this world, the disciples chosen on the foundation of truth, and even his own children.

"Father! Strike me and forgive everything." Yet, because Jesus carried grievances in such an environment, we must seek to resolve those grievances. After that, we must first repent personally, repent as a family, and then repent for our race, nation, and the world, saying, "If it is your will, I will bear any burden." We must be able to say, "I will take responsibility for sin and atone for it, and then I will walk the difficult and laborious path you have set before me." But what about Peter, John, and James? When faced with death, they packed their bags and fled. Is this the result left behind through his blood and his ideals? Therefore, it is those who can say they will go the path of death before the old Peter, James, and John who can become brides.

If you are a believer who wishes to become a bride in this world, you must stand before the enemies of God. In today's complex social environment, amidst numerous denominations fighting with each other, God desires someone who can discern which is true and can take responsibility for the many nations that are at war.

Until now, you may have said, "Father, please bless me," but the Unification Church is not such a place. Blessings are profoundly public. If you wish to receive blessings and become a bride, it cannot be for the individual. It must first be for heaven and earth. It is like preparing to marry in this world; you must prepare to fit into that household. But can you stand before God's prince, the Messiah of all mankind, and say, "Make me the first bride"?

Even now, God is engaged in a global struggle. Everyone, God is still fighting a global battle. Know this clearly. God fights not only for this nation but for many nations as well. Even now, the brink of death is looming. While you sleep, there are those who cannot sleep for God. If such a person exists, God must grieve for him, must pave his way, and must become a shield in his battle.

Those who wish to become brides must be unable to sleep comfortably for even one hour and must not be able to live comfortably for even one day. Moreover, those who wish to become brides must pray on behalf of the world, saying, "Father, strike me and forgive everything." Isn't that true in the world? A dutiful child, when their sibling has done wrong and the parents take up a whip, says, "Father, Mother, strike me and forgive my sibling."

From this perspective, we see that the essence of Christianity has changed. If there is a representative bride who can be called before God in this Korea, she must say, "Father! Please place upon me the sorrow of countless denominations and strike me." If you wish to become a bride representing the world, you must say, "Forgive everything in this world and strike me." You must be able to say, "If I alone am rejected, abandoned, and persecuted, but the entire humanity can live because of me, that is my glory and my wish."

Who would you choose as a bride: someone who says, "Good things are mine, yours are also mine, and mine is mine," or someone who is willing to take on the burden of the world?

When Jesus came to this earth and looked at the nation of Israel, they were already divided. If they had all said, "The blessings you bring are too heavy for us to bear," the world would have turned. The purpose of Jesus coming to this earth was not to burn everything but to restore the nation of Israel and save all mankind. Yet, he left without fulfilling that responsibility. At that time, his disciples were, in modern terms, arguing about who would be the left and right ministers. For Jesus, who was suffering and being persecuted, there was no place for such glory. The disciples did not understand that there was a path of persecution for Jesus.
With just two fish and five loaves, feeding five thousand people and still having leftovers, he thought that unifying the world would be no problem. 

The meaning contained in Jesus' historically final words
For Jesus, who had lost his nation and denomination, there remained a secondary path to be taken to restore them. To embark on this secondary path, it was necessary to determine the internal connections that God had labored over for four thousand years, as well as the external connections remaining with the denomination and nation. Despite this mission resting on Jesus, his disciples were completely unaware. What could those ignorant ones possibly know? How frustrating it must have been for him to say, "I still have much to say to you, but you cannot bear it now." How pitiful are those words!

The path Jesus walked was one of being chased by his nation, a path of suffering, a path of persecution, and a path of rebuilding the nation of Israel. To restore this nation of Israel, there remained a responsibility to fulfill the conditions that God had labored over for four thousand years to establish the nation of Israel and the Jewish denomination, yet all that existed were disciples who sought only glory. Thus, Jesus had no choice but to take on the historical connections of heaven and earth alone and go before the cross.

The suffering of Jesus on the cross
We must understand that the steps taken from the Garden of Gethsemane to Golgotha were steps taken to take responsibility for what the nation established could not, and what the disciples could not take responsibility for. 

You must think about how great the sorrow of Jesus hanging on the cross was. Darkness fell over the whole earth just before Jesus died. While hanging on the cross, Jesus cried out, "My God, my God, why have you forsaken me?" He was forsaken by God. How miserable is that? The Messiah, who had been sent after four thousand years of guiding providence, had to turn his face away from the cross at that moment. How could Jesus, who came as the prince of God, leave behind such a tragic statement, "My God, my God, why have you forsaken me?" This is a blemish in the history of humanity. It is a historical blemish.

Today, countless Christians scattered around the world have a path to follow. What path is that? To resolve the sorrow left by Jesus at Golgotha, we must shed tears and sweat. When Jesus carried the cross and saw the women following him weeping, he said, "Do not weep for me, but weep for yourselves and for your children." This is true. My tears remain for humanity. The path I take to the cross does not end here; it is a historical path of the cross. If I go as an individual, my responsibility ends, but after I go, your responsibilities remain. Therefore, personal responsibility, familial responsibility, tribal responsibility, national responsibility, global responsibility, and cosmic responsibility remain. To fulfill that responsibility, countless Christians must walk the path of tears and the path of the cross. 

The Jesus who carried such a heavy cross worked hard to prepare a foundation on this earth where God could dwell, even while feeling the injustice of having to reflect on history, touch the world, or repent for the past. 

You must understand that when Jesus on the cross said, "My God, my God, why have you forsaken me?" it was not merely a personal lament. It was a statement made as the Messiah with a great mission. It was fine to be forsaken, but he pleaded that the countless people who had been with him should not be forsaken. Do not forsake Peter, do not forsake John the Baptist, do not forsake the twelve disciples, do not forsake the nation of Israel, and do not forsake the countless Christians who will come in the future. This was the historical final word of Jesus.

To meet the Messiah
As Christians who must follow such a path, we must reach the point of pleading before the Father, "I embrace the nation and struggle for it, so please do not forsake the nation. I hold onto this world and struggle for it, so please do not forsake this world."

Again, we must understand how great the pain of Jesus on the cross was. The Jesus on the cross looked to heaven, and everything was dark before him. Looking at the earth was also dark, and looking at humanity was dark as well. It was overwhelmingly dark. Yet, even in such darkness, the one thought that arose was, "Why have you forsaken me?" Within that statement was a plea, "O God, do not forsake me forever. It is natural for humanity to be forsaken because of Adam and Eve, but please do not forsake the labor you have put into history. Do not forsake what you have worked so hard for. Even if you forsake me, do not forsake the hope you had to establish through this nation. Do not forsake the ideal you had to govern all people through this nation."

We must understand that this was the heartfelt prayer of Jesus. I may go, but what will happen to your will? I may not have been able to fulfill the duty of a loyal subject for you, but I have a loyal heart. I may not have been able to fulfill the duty of a filial son, but I have a heart of filial piety. However, in this land, if even such a person is forsaken, what will happen?

This is not a prayer lamenting one's own existence. It is historical. It is a plea embracing the Father who has labored until now. Because this single-mindedness touched the heart of the Father, the powers of recreation and resurrection were unleashed. 

Moreover, when Jesus prayed, "Do not hold their sins against them," it was a prayer born out of love, considering above all the labor of God. If you forsake them, what will happen to God's will? Even if I walk the path of death a thousand or ten thousand times, if you forsake them, the fruits of God's labor will be shattered. This is what Jesus was pleading for.

What saddens us today? It is why our ancestors treated the Messiah, who came after four thousand years, in such a shabby manner. What Christians today should be angry about is the actions of Peter, James, and John, these three disciples. Even for a nation in the world, one would not act that way. How could they act that way when their master, whom they served, was walking the path of death?

To meet the Messiah, one must willingly walk the path of death. If you wish to embrace the resurrected Lord as your bridegroom, you must first pass over the hill of the cross and be resurrected. This is the truth. To find what was lost, one must go to the place where it was lost. Today, there remains a historical cross because of Jesus' cross. Because of the cross, the historical sorrow of Jesus remains. Because of the cross, the essence of Jesus' sorrow becomes a sacrifice. For this reason, through individuals, families, tribes, and nations, God seeks to establish a sovereign nation to restore this world. Therefore, Christianity, which must restore the second phase, seeks to do so in the name of Jesus and the Holy Spirit. Here, Jesus and the Holy Spirit must work again. They must labor for a long time to find and establish one person. To establish a family, they must labor with the ideal that Abraham had. To establish a nation, they must endure more suffering than the Israelites did in Egypt. Thus, the history of Christianity up to now has been a re-enactment of the miserable environment that the nation of Israel fell into two thousand years ago.

The Jesus who came to this earth is a historical reality. He is the reality of historical hope. Therefore, he is the reality that the ancient Adam hoped for, the reality of the promise made to Noah, the reality that represented Noah's painful circumstances, and the reality that spoke for Noah's heart, as well as for Abraham and even for John the Baptist of that era. 

So, what was the reason Jesus endured the pain on the cross, biting his tongue and clenching his teeth? He walked through history and inwardly appealed. "I will not be like Adam. I will not be like Adam, who sowed the seeds of disbelief on this earth. I will not be like Cain, who killed his brother whom he should have loved. Even in a position where I could kill, I will forgive."

You must understand that if you had been born as Noah's own son at that time, you would have cursed him for building the ark for 120 years. "Why build a boat on top of a mountain? Shouldn't it be built by the riverside or the seaside?" It was not that he deliberately wanted to avoid any help from the world; it was to change the world. To teach God's will to his wife and children, fundamentally, evangelism had to take place. Even if the whole nation and everyone who had their eyes opened rejected him, he had to stand before the will. He could not become a captive before them.

At that time, Noah's wife would have come before dawn, saying, "Sir, the time for building the ark is running late, so please get up. We need to pray at dawn, so hurry up." Can you imagine that? Think about it, ladies. If you made a Korean woman suffer for just a year, she wouldn't just complain; she would grab you by the collar! Would that have happened? Think about it. It has been 120 years. But God had to make it that way.

And what about his three sons? "Oh! Our father is holy. This is God's command, so please do it." Do you think they would have said that? How could they have known whether they heard God's command? Would God have told Noah, "Noah, there will definitely be difficulties"? But Noah, having received a command once, persevered through storms for 120 years and carried it through to the end. "Strike him, betray him, let your companions oppose him," and only after establishing conditions suitable for punishing him did the judgment come. Jesus is the embodiment of Noah, who built the ark. Even if faced with the slander and ridicule of countless people, even if it cost him his life, he declared that his determined heart would not change. This is loyalty.

Abraham was also called out by God from a luxurious environment as the son of Terah, an idol merchant. He was told to leave his beloved hometown. He was to become a people without a nation, a child without parents. He was to break all attachments centered around relatives and family. Because Abraham had a revolutionary heart that loathed his father being an idol merchant and wondered if there was no way to change this, God saw that and called him out. When he was called out, he was useful. So, he was told, "Offer a sacrifice. Offer your son Isaac, whom you bore at a hundred years old." And he said, "Yes." 

Think about it. Wasn't that madness? Even if one is mad, one should be mad in the right way; this was madness in the wrong way, right? 

When Jesus thought of such things, he stood in the position of being the representative of Adam, Abel, Noah, Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob, and he resolved to be a true parent to the children of faith. Even on the cross, he said, "If my body can be a sacrifice to fulfill the will of the Father, I will die a thousand times, ten thousand times."

When Jesus prayed, "My Father, if it is possible, let this cup pass from me. Yet not as I will, but as you will," it was not because Jesus wanted to live. It is eternally connected and eternally reciprocal, so even if one brings out just one standard from that, there is nothing that cannot be integrated or responded to. Therefore, we must advance to the position of the victorious subject centered on such a standard of love. Until now, humans have not been able to find such a position, which is why we are seeking it.

Because fallen humans have lost hope, they must find the reality centered on faith and connect it to love. God has been waiting for someone who can claim to be a dutiful child, a loyal subject, and a virtuous woman before Him until now.

Anyone who first enters the Unification Church and hears the Principle words becomes so engrossed in the words that they forget about their home. They also become disconnected from the world. Their beloved husband and beloved children become bothersome. They become so busy with their own path that everything except those words becomes bothersome. A person who does not feel this is a dead person.

The Lord who is coming will be the victorious subject in hope representing God, the victorious subject in faith, and the victorious subject in love. Therefore, God says that when such a person appears, He will give all people to them. Once that position is determined, He will give the 3 billion people of humanity to them. He will give all authority to them. Everything must go through them. From that, the order of heaven will be established, and the nations and the world will also be ordered.

God has given this privilege to the ancestors of humanity, but because they lost it, they had to trace the path of restoration. So, what kind of process must be gone through to find this path? One must go through the path of sorrow, the path of suffering, and the path of death. Why? Because today's world remains in the valley of sorrow, suffering, and death. To resolve this, all of these must be overcome.

The process that the victorious subject must go through is not found at once. One must collide and clash with everything countless times. Pure gold becomes cleaner the more times it is put into the fire; it does not become dirtier. Similarly, to reach such a standard, one must go through a difficult historical course. Otherwise, one cannot transcend. To break through, one must carry personal crosses, family crosses, tribal crosses, national crosses, and global crosses.

For this reason, the one who must come as the subject of all things is the most pitiful person on this earth from an individual perspective. Until they establish the standard of victory, they are a pitiful person. They are pitiful even at the family level, and they go through the pitiful standards until they pass through tribal, national, and global stages. However, even if they are sad or in pain, they are the ones responsible for establishing God's victory, and they carry the responsibility to establish God's victory even on the path of death.

The coming Lord must bear not only personal sorrow and pain but also national sorrow and pain, and even global sorrow and pain. They must accept the path of death for all people. They are called to become the victorious subjects of victory on this earth. They must not be defeated by the sorrow of the world but become victorious subjects who can be grateful even if they bear greater sorrow. They must become the victorious subjects centered on pain and the victorious subjects centered on death, even if they suffer at the boundary of death. This must be achieved in all directions. Only then can they become the victorious subjects centered on God's wishes and hopes, the victorious subjects centered on faith, and the victorious subjects centered on love.

Therefore, you must also do the same. You must exert more effort than anyone else, invest more sincerity than anyone else, and fight more fiercely than anyone else. This is a path that cannot be taken without going through such a process. In any case, this is a path that cannot be avoided.

The trial period of three times or more
Today, God may seem truly ruthless. God only teaches the path when someone arises who can help. This shows that God does not govern with just one generation but governs within three generations. He does not only need Adam and Eve but seeks to establish their son to match the three numbers. Whenever God is the subject, there must always be a counterpart that goes through three numbers. Therefore, even if He teaches, the important matters are taught through the three numbers. If you believe well in what is taught through the three numbers, it becomes yours. If you manage it well, it becomes yours.

When looking at all things centered on heaven and earth, where there is heaven and earth, there must be a person. Just as there are heaven and earth, the Trinity is the same. One cannot do it alone. One must establish the three numbers. When one must find themselves, they must necessarily need descendants, descendants they can connect to on this earth. Therefore, if one raises sons and daughters well, only then will they be taught. If they grow well, only then will they be taught the path of heaven.

As much as God has raised me, when one invests their sincerity and struggles for one life, they will be taught. Therefore, you must long for your family to the point where you cannot sleep at night. Sorrow does not only come from external calamities. Loneliness is also sorrowful. It is sorrowful when one knows the will but has no one to boast about it. Sorrow can arise from external pain and calamity, but it can also arise when there is no one to convey the internal loneliness or will.

However, even while in such circumstances, one must not betray God or neglect their responsibilities. When God makes a decision, He always establishes Cain and Abel. He teaches through Cain. From this perspective, sorrow, pain, and the path of death must be pioneered by oneself. One must endure to the end and pioneer through it; that is the path of restoration. For this reason, Jesus also died on the cross, resurrected, established the hope of victory, and sent the Holy Spirit. From here, a decisive start was made, and Christianity was established as a global movement.

God has continued this history. In the process of such history, God may seem unfeeling. It is not certain whether God exists or not. However, in such circumstances, one must have a heart that believes and relies on God, and they must be prepared to overcome the paths of sorrow, pain, and death.

You must be prepared to face death at least three times. You must overcome the place of death more than three times. You must understand that by going through such places, you can become the victorious subject who can face God's love.

Therefore, you must carry the belief that you can establish the victorious authority even on the paths of sorrow, pain, and death. When I started this path, I prepared for death hundreds of times. There was a period of trials. There is a training period where one commands themselves. Thus, one must overcome the national death hill, the national pain hill, and the national sorrow hill, and they must experience the global death calamity, global pain calamity, and global sorrow calamity. Furthermore, when heaven and earth are sorrowful and struggling at the crossroads of life and death, it is the path of restoration to resolve this and pave the way for victory.

Jesus only resolved the spiritual aspect while struggling through the national and global paths of death, sorrow, and pain. Even so, one must carry God's wishes and love in the sad place, in the painful place, and in the place of death, and they must develop the ability to manifest as that reality. Only then can they become the sovereign of hope or the sovereign of love who completes God's restoration providence in the end.

The Savior has come
<Prayer (I)> This morning is the first Sabbath of the new year 1965 and also the day marking the 1965th year of the Lord's incarnation. Countless people have celebrated the birth of the Messiah on their own terms, without knowing what kind of connections and values the Messiah established with humanity, the world, and the universe after coming to this earth, only remembering His fame and celebrating the birth of the Messiah. 
However, the few gathered here today are those who, 2,000 years ago, were sent by your vast and high will and dignified providence in the person of Jesus, but we cannot help but feel sympathy for the unfortunate circumstances he faced, and we cannot help but painfully reflect on the fact that the Israelite people did not fulfill their mission at that time. Moreover, when we think of the sad heart of the Father, who was anxious about the Israelite people and Judaism not fulfilling their national mission, we must remember once again the sorrowful heart of the Father, who had no choice but to send the promised Messiah as the time and season have come. 
We understand that the one who was born on this earth as your precious son was sent to resolve the sorrow of losing Adam, who abandoned the ideals of creation. Through him, you sought to fulfill your will, receive glory, and establish the world of happiness, and it was the Messiah you sent to accomplish that hope. 
Jesus was born in a humble manner from the day he was born. Many people waited and longed for the Messiah, but they did not recognize the one who came as the Messiah. This Messiah had to live with the heart of God and carry the hope of God alone, appearing in a humble form and ultimately suffering on the cross, shedding tears and blood. When we think of this, we cannot help but apologize for the shortcomings of our ancestors, and we must confess the sin of the Judaism that failed to fulfill its mission and betrayed God. We must take this time to deeply reflect on the history of sin that has caused our ancestors to shed blood throughout history and the sins of humanity that have betrayed God. 
We understand that only those who can joyfully welcome the day the Messiah comes are those who bear the sorrows that the Messiah must endure. It is our duty to celebrate the birth of the one who came to this earth and played a role in establishing one ideal, and we must ask ourselves when we have ever welcomed him in such a position, shed tears for him, or devoted ourselves and moved our hands in loyalty for him. When have we ever worked for you in such a position? The more we think about it, the more we realize that no matter what we do, we cannot repay the sorrowful and pitiful facts. 
Father! We must take care of your sorrow, we must sympathize with the unjust circumstances of Jesus, and we must become those who can understand the miserable and pitiful circumstances of his disciples who have walked the bloody path until now. 
Two thousand years of history have passed. How many sad circumstances have there been during that time? The Father has been sad, Jesus has been sad, the Holy Spirit has been sad, and Christians have been sad. We also know that the final day, the day of judgment that everyone is looking forward to, is approaching to resolve this deep sorrow. The saints of this end time, who are in a position to welcome the Messiah who comes to resolve the accumulated sorrow of the Father, must not only wait for the coming Messiah like the Israelite people who longed for him but must each prepare their hearts to serve the coming Messiah. 
On this day, may the Father bless us. We have not prepared anything, but we offer our anxious hearts and wounded bodies to your altar, and we sincerely hope that this time will allow us to feel the life of Jesus, who suffered, and to empathize with the life of Jesus who walked the path of the cross. 
We know that many numbers are not the issue. Before there is a nation, there must be a people; before there is a people, there must be a tribe; before there is a tribe, there must be a family; and before there is a family, there must be an individual. Jesus came to this earth without a nation, without a people, without a tribe, without a family, and without even the dignity of his own person. We understand that there were no true disciples who recognized him as the Messiah of the tribe, people, nation, and world, and there were no families. 
Now, as we must welcome the Messiah who will come again, we must receive the recognition of the Messiah from a personal standpoint, from a family standpoint, and from a collective standpoint responsible for the tribe, people, and nation. We must think of this tremendous task that remains before us and attend this gathering with a longing heart. 
We must not forget that the overall purpose of commemorating the birth of the Messiah today is to personally comfort Jesus, to comfort him as a family, to comfort him nationally, and to comfort him globally. 
Today, our knees that bow here are weak knees, our bodies are wounded bodies, and we are bodies that cannot show our faces before the Father for both the past and present. However, we know that you have been guiding us with a heart of compassion throughout history, and we recognize that you were concerned for humanity in that moment when the Messiah was destined. Please remember us who bow here. 
We do not wish to seek you and call upon you in a glamorous position like others. We embrace our hearts that are anxious and filled with tears, and we long for you, Father.
the Jewish leaders should have united to welcome the Messiah sent by God, but instead, they became the primary instigators in driving Jesus away, aligning themselves with the Roman soldiers, Pilate, and King Herod to kill Him.

The Israelite people and the Jewish community, who were meant to be prepared to receive the Messiah, failed to do so, resulting in a historical tragedy that cannot be denied. Two thousand years ago, the Messiah came to meet the Israelite people, the Jewish community, and the leaders of Judea, who were prepared by God. After four thousand years of a bloody struggle, the Israelites, who had suffered, been oppressed, and chased, were led by the Jewish community, and God could not help but send the Messiah to them.

Additionally, according to the principle of indemnity, God, who governs based on numerical standards, sent the Messiah at the appointed time, even though the nation was not prepared to take responsibility for that era. The long history of four thousand years had reached a point where God could send the Messiah centered on one purpose.

So, what was the purpose of sending the Messiah? It was to meet the Israelite people and to live a heavenly life centered on the ideology of the Messiah alongside them. Thus, it was to leave a brilliant historical tradition in the history of the Israelite people centered on God's will and the new concept of the Messiah. This tradition was to inherit God's wishes, circumstances, and heart, and to liberate God. Therefore, we must understand that it was the responsibility of the Messiah to bring God to a resting place.

The Messiah came to find the Israelite people. He came to find Judaism, the religious foundation that guides the Israelite people. He came to meet the high priests and the teachers of the law of Judaism. It is certain that the Messiah came to meet them.

Then, the upper and lower echelons should have united to meet the Messiah. At that time, the Jewish nation was a vassal state of Rome, and because of their enmity with Rome, the national leaders who were striving to restore the sovereignty of their devastated nation, as well as the religious leaders, should have united against Rome based on the new ideology of the Messiah. This was the attitude that the leaders of Judaism and the Jewish nation should have taken at that time. However, when the Messiah came, the leaders of the Jewish community and the Israelite people became the first instigators in driving Him away and sought to kill Him, aligning themselves with the Roman soldiers, Pilate, and King Herod.

The Israelite people and the Jewish community, who were meant to be prepared to receive the Messiah sent by God, should have united in joy to welcome Jesus. Instead, they became the very ones who rejected Him.
the Messiah had to unite on the ideology of the Messiah on behalf of countless nations and become one before the will of God. This was the responsibility of the Jewish community and the Jewish nation. However, because they failed in this responsibility, we know that the Messiah Jesus walked a miserable path.

Joseph and Mary and Jesus
Jesus was born in a stable. He went through a preparation period of about 30 years. After that, during his three years of public ministry, he tried to establish his purpose but ultimately failed and was crucified. When we think about the life of Jesus over those 30 years, we can see that he never had the authority of the Messiah on this earth, even for a single day. From the moment he was born until his death, he did not have the environment of a Messiah sent by God, nor did he have a family or relatives. Even John the Baptist, the forerunner prepared by God for that era, did not welcome him, nor did the prophets of that time. Throughout his entire life, there was not a single person among the entire nation who treated him as the Messiah. Because of this, he must have carried the sorrow of not being recognized as an individual, the sorrow of not being welcomed as a family member, and perhaps the sorrow of not being acknowledged by his tribe, nation, or country.

In this context, as we commemorate the birth of the Messiah, we should understand the life of the Messiah who came with hope but left with sorrow, rather than just celebrating the Messiah who came to this earth with hope. Otherwise, I believe there is no true meaning in celebrating the day the Messiah was born.

God had to send the Messiah to a family, so He chose the family of Joseph. The family of Joseph and Mary was the family that God embraced. When the angel announced to the virgin Mary that she would conceive as a virgin, Mary initially rejected it. However, after hearing the angel's repeated encouragement, she said, "I am the Lord's servant; may your word to me be fulfilled." Mary, who was prepared to make any sacrifice for the glory of the Messiah, was able to conceive the Messiah. From the day Joseph learned that Mary was pregnant, he was troubled. It was impossible for Joseph not to be troubled when his betrothed was with child. This was something that could not be accepted in the social context of that time or according to the Law of Moses. In this troubled state, the angel of the Lord appeared to Joseph in a dream and commanded him, "Do not be afraid to take Mary home as your wife." Upon hearing this, Joseph did not hesitate to take Mary, valuing God's command above all else.

Thus, Mary and Joseph, who began a journey unlike any other in the world, had the responsibility of raising a child unlike any other. This was the responsibility of the Joseph family. Since the nation did not accept Jesus as the Messiah, Joseph had to embrace Jesus, who was like a stepson, as the Messiah on behalf of the nation. This was the responsibility that lay upon Joseph. Similarly, Mary had the responsibility to treat Jesus, the Messiah who came in the name of her husband, as the highest bride of the universe, embodying the essence of the ultimate bride from the very beginning. This was God's original purpose in sending the Messiah to that family, but Joseph and Mary failed to fulfill that mission.

In terms of familial standards, Jesus was sent to a family more precious than any other, as a being more valuable than any noble person in Israel, a Savior whom one could not exchange for heaven and earth. If Mary and Joseph had truly recognized and honored Jesus, his life would not have been a sorrowful one. Today, while the Catholic Church venerates the Virgin Mary, if Mary had fulfilled her mission as Jesus' mother, Jesus would not have had to suffer so much. If Joseph had followed the example of Mary, who devoted herself to fulfilling God's will, and had centered his life around Jesus, he would not have had to suffer so much.

Joseph should have understood that, although Jesus was in the position of his son, in essence, he was not. From a superficial worldly perspective, Jesus and Joseph had a father-son relationship, but in terms of purpose, they had a master-servant relationship. From the very beginning, their paths and essences were different, weren't they? Therefore, from the moment Joseph recognized Jesus as the Messiah, he should have faithfully fulfilled the priestly mission of serving Jesus above all else. Furthermore, Joseph's sons and daughters, that is, Jesus' siblings, should have obeyed Jesus, their older brother, more than anyone else.

Jesus' words were those that the entire Jewish nation should have upheld, and they should have recognized that they were words to which they must obey, even disregarding the doctrines and laws centered on the Pentateuch. If they had done so, Jesus would not have lived a sorrowful family life and would have been welcomed both personally and as a family member. However, because the Joseph family did not welcome Jesus as a family member, Jesus could not find a position to be welcomed personally or as a family member.

When Jesus came to this earth, he came through the family of Joseph, right? Joseph was a descendant of David. This means he had a bloodline with a historical connection to the faithful ancestors who established the path of loyalty to fulfill God's will. From the day Joseph met the important Messiah, he should have cast aside all past mistakes and centered his life around the Messiah. If Joseph had lived this way, Peter would not have been necessary. If Joseph had created a resting place in a familial environment, there would have been no need for Jesus to go out into the world. Ignorant Peter, James, and John should not have been Jesus' disciples; rather, Jesus' beloved siblings should have been his disciples. That is how I understand it.

The Joseph family should have been the protective fence for Jesus. God labored for thousands of years to establish the nation of Israel and to give birth to the Messiah from that chosen bloodline. The Messiah could not abandon that bloodline and govern. However, Jesus could not hold Joseph's hand or Mary's hand and say, "This is my will and desire." This was the greatest tragedy in Jesus' life.

Jesus, who was born on this earth as the Messiah, was born through Mary's womb but did not receive a mother's love. Although he was born through Mary's physical body like any other person, when we consider Jesus' ideology and mission, Mary was not his mother. He had to establish a foundation for rest based on family, making that family a refuge and a place of comfort, gathering relatives and tribes, and creating a foundation that would not collapse even if the nation opposed him, from which Jesus could begin his public ministry.

However, during the 30 years of preparation, what did Jesus look forward to? Jesus loved his family more than he loved the nation. He loved Joseph and Mary more than he loved God's will. That love was not superficial. Jesus loved his parents through the heart of God, through the historical heart, through the heart of the times, and even with concern for the future.

To me, Mary was my mother, who bore me by God's command. Jesus, the Messiah, longed for a mother's love. He longed for a father's love. Wouldn't he?

Joseph, although he was Jesus' stepfather, should have loved Jesus more than his own children. Jesus' siblings knew what their older brother was trying to become, even if he did not say it. Who understood the sorrow of Jesus, who could not treat his parents as parents, or the sorrow of Jesus, who could not treat his siblings as siblings, or the sorrow of Jesus, who could not embrace his relatives as relatives? This was Jesus' tragedy. Moreover, it is extremely tragic that Christianity, which does not understand these things, venerates Jesus as the Messiah. The Nature of God and Satan
By carrying out all of God’s commands, Abraham was in a position where God could say, "From you..." To establish such a position, God sought out Abraham. Thus, God commanded Abraham to leave behind his beloved homeland and pack his belongings to depart from Ur of the Chaldeans to a new land. He told him to leave behind his loving parents, family, and tribe. Following such a command from God was a venture for Abraham.

Anyone would feel sorrow when parting from their parents. However, no matter how precious the foundation of that family life has been until now, it cannot be helped. No matter how precious one's environment, tribal foundation, or national foundation may be, it must all be abandoned. When leaving, one must not think, "Oh! I am going to live well." The blessing that God bestowed upon Abraham, saying, "Your descendants will be as numerous as the stars in the sky and the grains of sand by the sea," was not a blessing for just Abraham's single family. It was not a blessing to make Abraham prosperous or to give him wealth. The blessing promised to Abraham as an individual was a historical blessing for the world. Although it was a blessing given to Abraham as an individual, it was a blessing given to Abraham as a representative of the world, so it was a blessing that could unfold the eternal and unchanging will. Therefore, that blessing includes family, tribe, nation, and the world.

When Abraham received God’s blessing, he did not understand the meaning of that blessing. Yet, when God later commanded him to offer his only son Isaac as a burnt offering, he took Isaac and went up to Mount Moriah to offer the sacrifice. Consider this from a realistic standpoint today. It might seem that God has lost His mind. However, the reason God commanded Abraham to do such a thing was to judge history and the era. Even if Abraham's descendants were to perish in history, through the life foundation and actions established by Abraham, an absolute standard was to be set so that they could live blessed forever. If God were to exclude humanity from establishing a great will because humanity has fallen, then Satan would attack humanity based on that condition. We ourselves are children of sin. However, because we are called and corrected and we face a purpose greater than that sin, God forgives us.

In this way, we can see God's attitude throughout His providential history. I do not know how many days the teacher will stay here, but I hope you will become one even after the teacher leaves Japan. We have received life through the good lineage recognized by our God, born in this land of Japan by precious connections. Unknowingly, we were born on this earth with a purpose, hope, and desire where God is present. That is contributing something to our ancestors, and considering that God's desire is being fulfilled where we believe, we cannot blame human shortcomings.

As we move under even greater connections, relationships, and desires, and purposes, standing at the forefront for the development of Japan, without losing heart, not knowing fatigue, and not considering difficulties as difficulties, for those who stand as a historical and heavenly revolutionary to save the world, such a cross is not a problem. Such difficulties can occur, and that is the truth. This is the path of destiny that one must take. If one goes with such thoughts, I believe that the land of Japan will experience remarkable development.

Become a warrior of the restoration of heaven and earth
Now, let me conclude. As a warrior of the restoration of heaven and earth, crossing over the end of the world with the purpose in front of you, offering the resolution of the restoration of heaven and earth before God, as a being of value greater than the creation of heaven and earth, God is waiting for one person who can stand before all creation, saying, "I am a true person who loves you, a loyal person who loves you." Have you ever truly thought about the restoration of heaven and earth?

What is the heaven of the restoration of heaven and earth? What is the lord of the restoration? What is the restoration, the concept of restoration that we can feel in our consciousness? When God commands that the earth must follow this course for some reason in the vast universe, it must revolve infinitely; God is an absolute deity.

When thinking about this infinite universe, light travels at a speed of 300,000 kilometers per second, and the distance it travels in a year is called a light-year in astronomy. The universe is so vast that there are still lights that have not yet reached the earth even after traveling for more than 6 billion years. Consider that infinite universe. It is unimaginably vast. Everything is under the law of connection, having infinite relationships, creating a world of one purpose amid an unbreakable hope. When thinking about that, not only the present but also the past, when considering God Himself who moves this vast universe, have you ever thought about whether that God is truly our Father? When He comes to us with tears and says, "Oh, so-and-so! I am your true Father. I am your true parent," if there is a true parent who can embrace us, is there anything more glorious, anything more reassuring that can be obtained as a human being? We call Him Father, and we are loved by Him.
